# raftexample\\n2: \\n3: raftexample is an example usage of etcd's [raft library](https://github.com/etcd-io/raft). Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n52: // your own risk.\n53: package leaderelection\n54: \n55: import (\n56: \t\"bytes\"\n57: \t\"context\"\n58: \t\"fmt\"\n59: \t\"sync\"\n60: \t\"time\"\n61: \n62: \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n67: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n68: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n69: )\n70: \n71: const (\n72: \tJitterFactor = 1.2\n73: )\n74: \n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n77: \tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n78: \t\treturn LeaderElector{\n108: \t\tconfig:  lec,\n109: \t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n110: \t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n111: \t}\n112: \tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n113: **distributed lease-based leader election** mechanism through its client-go library, primarily used by control plane components like the scheduler and controller-manager.\\n\\n**Core Architecture:**\\n- **Resource Lock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go): Defines the abstraction for leader election resources supporting Get, Create, and Update operations\\n- **LeaseLock Implementation** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): Uses Kubernetes Lease API objects (v1.coordination.k8s.io) to store election state with fields: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n- **LeaderElector** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go): Main client managing the election lifecycle with configurable timers (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod)\\n\\n**Election Algorithm:**\\n1. **Acquisition Phase (acquire method)**: Calls tryAcquireOrRenew repeatedly with jitter-based backoff until successful\\n2. **Fast Path Renewal**: If already leading and lease is valid, optimistically renews the lease\\n3. **Slow Path Renewal**: Fetches current lease record, checks expiration (LeaseDurationSeconds), and updates if still valid\\n4. **Lease Expiration Detection**: Uses local observedTime + LeaseDurationSeconds to detect lease timeout\\n5. **Release/Failover**: On context cancellation or renewal failure, calls release() to set LeaseDurationSeconds=1 for quick re-election\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- Non-leader candidates continuously poll the lease resource (RetryPeriod intervals)\\n- When a lease expires (no renewal within LeaseDurationSeconds), candidates can immediately acquire it\\n- LeaderTransitions counter tracks leadership changes for monitoring\\n- Health check integration via HealthzAdaptor enables graceful shutdown notification\\n- Coordinated Leader Election (optional, v1beta1) allows multiple candidates to negotiate succession\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n- Clock-skew tolerant (configurable LeaseDuration vs RenewDeadline ratio)\\n- No external consensus required - uses Kubernetes API as storage\\n- Supports timeout-based and event-driven detection\\n- Records holder identity, acquisition time, and renewal time\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through **Raft consensus** at two levels: the core cluster membership protocol and a client-facing election API.\\n\\n**Raft Consensus Layer** (Embedded in etcd):\\n- **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Manages the Raft state machine with election timeout based on ElectionTicks\\n- **Raft States**: Follower, Candidate, Leader (managed by go.etcd.io/raft/v3 library)\\n- **Leader Election Trigger**: Election occurs when no heartbeat received within ElectionTimeout (ElectionTicks × TickMs milliseconds)\\n- **Pre-Vote Optimization** (server/config/config.go): Reduces disruptive elections when nodes rejoin; candidates first ask for votes without updating term\\n- **Initial Election Tick Advance**: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to accelerate initial leader election (configurable via --initial-election-tick-advance flag)\\n\\n**Election Timeout Calculation** (server/config/config.go):\\n- ElectionTimeout = ElectionTicks × TickMs (default: 10 ticks × 100ms = 1 second)\\n- Automatic adjustment on server restart to prevent disruptive re-elections\\n\\n**Client-Facing Election API** (server/etcdserver/api/v3election/):\\n- **Campaign**: Place a candidate in the election, wait for previous leader's deletion via watchDeletes()\\n- **Proclaim**: Leader updates its value in the election using transactional compare-and-set with CreateRevision check\\n- **Resign**: Leader voluntarily steps down by deleting its key\\n- **Leader**: Query current election leader by getting first key with WithFirstCreate ordering\\n- **Observe**: Stream ordered leader proclamations as they occur\\n\\nThe gRPC service (v3election.proto) wraps concurrency.Election client through server-side session management.\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n1. **Leader Failure Detection**: Followers detect leader absence when heartbeat messages stop arriving\\n2. **Timeout-Triggered Election**: After ElectionTimeout, followers become candidates and request votes\\n3. **Consensus-Based Selection**: Only candidates with majority votes become leaders (Raft guarantees)\\n4. **Automatic Log Replication**: New leader pulls missing log entries from followers before committing\\n5. **ensureLeadership()** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Verifies leadership via linearizable read; checks raftStatus().Lead equals local MemberID\\n6. **Leadership Transfer**: Graceful handoff when leader steps down\\n\\n**Raft Message Transport** (server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/transport.go):\\n- HTTP/2 based peer-to-peer transport for Raft messages\\n- LeaderStats tracks replication progress to followers\\n- Separate optimized stream for heartbeat AppendEntries messages from leaders\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Distributed lease with API-based storage | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease objects (etcd or external) | In-memory Raft log + persistent WAL |\\n| **Leader Detection** | Polling-based (RetryPeriod) | Heartbeat timeouts (ElectionTicks) |\\n| **Failover Time** | Configurable (LeaseDuration, default 15s) | Bounded by ElectionTimeout (default 1s) |\\n| **Consistency** | Eventual consistency via API | Strong consistency via Raft quorum |\\n| **Scalability** | Limited by API server throughput | Peer-to-peer consensus independent of API |\\n| **Election Coordination** | Sequential leasing with renewal | Parallel voting with quorum requirement |\\n| **Monitoring** | Via LeaderElectionRecord metadata | Via Raft metrics and LeaderStats |\\n\\n### Election State Tracking\\n\\n**Kubernetes LeaderElectionRecord** fields:\\n- HolderIdentity: Current leader ID\\n- AcquireTime: When leadership was acquired\\n- RenewTime: Last renewal timestamp\\n- LeaseDurationSeconds: Lease validity period\\n- LeaderTransitions: Count of leadership changes\\n- PreferredHolder: Next leader candidate (coordinated election)\\n- Strategy: Election strategy being used\\n\\n**etcd Raft Election** state:\\n- raftStatus.Lead: Current leader node ID\\n- raftStatus.Term: Current election term\\n- raftStatus.State: Node's state (Follower/Candidate/Leader)\\n- Raft log: Command sequence establishing consensus\\n- Lease ID: Associated session lease for key holding\\n\\n### Failover and Re-Election Triggers\\n\\n**Kubernetes Triggers:**\\n1. Lease.RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds < current time\\n2. Explicit release (ReleaseOnCancel=true on context cancel)\\n3. Failed Update operations\\n4. LeaderTransitions threshold (coordinated election mode)\\n\\n**etcd Triggers:**\\n1. No heartbeat messages within ElectionTimeout\\n2. Leadership transfer request (Leader.TransferLeadership)\\n3. Configuration changes (membership changes trigger re-election)\\n4. Explicit resignation via Election.Resign() API\\n\\nBoth systems ensure safe, deterministic leadership transitions through either time-based leasing (k8s) or consensus voting (etcd), with proper handling of network partitions and cascading failures.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2136,"cache_read_input_tokens":89604,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2136},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2bd4c01d-a08b-4468-9179-6697a7fa3936","uuid":"313fc5e5-4593-43fa-8803-75b656e7497b"}

\"symbol\": \"ensureLeadership\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Pattern Comparison: Kubernetes vs etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements a **distributed lease-based leader election** mechanism through its client-go library, primarily used by control plane components like the scheduler and controller-manager.\\n\\n**Core Architecture:**\\n- **Resource Lock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go): Defines the abstraction for leader election resources supporting Get, Create, and Update operations\\n- **LeaseLock Implementation** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): Uses Kubernetes Lease API objects (v1.coordination.k8s.io) to store election state with fields: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n- **LeaderElector** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go): Main client managing the election lifecycle with configurable timers (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod)\\n\\n**Election Algorithm:**\\n1. **Acquisition Phase (acquire method)**: Calls tryAcquireOrRenew repeatedly with jitter-based backoff until successful\\n2. **Fast Path Renewal**: If already leading and lease is valid, optimistically renews the lease\\n3. **Slow Path Renewal**: Fetches current lease record, checks expiration (LeaseDurationSeconds), and updates if still valid\\n4. **Lease Expiration Detection**: Uses local observedTime + LeaseDurationSeconds to detect lease timeout\\n5. **Release/Failover**: On context cancellation or renewal failure, calls release() to set LeaseDurationSeconds=1 for quick re-election\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- Non-leader candidates continuously poll the lease resource (RetryPeriod intervals)\\n- When a lease expires (no renewal within LeaseDurationSeconds), candidates can immediately acquire it\\n- LeaderTransitions counter tracks leadership changes for monitoring\\n- Health check integration via HealthzAdaptor enables graceful shutdown notification\\n- Coordinated Leader Election (optional, v1beta1) allows multiple candidates to negotiate succession\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n- Clock-skew tolerant (configurable LeaseDuration vs RenewDeadline ratio)\\n- No external consensus required - uses Kubernetes API as storage\\n- Supports timeout-based and event-driven detection\\n- Records holder identity, acquisition time, and renewal time\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through **Raft consensus** at two levels: the core cluster membership protocol and a client-facing election API.\\n\\n**Raft Consensus Layer** (Embedded in etcd):\\n- **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Manages the Raft state machine with election timeout based on ElectionTicks\\n- **Raft States**: Follower, Candidate, Leader (managed by go.etcd.io/raft/v3 library)\\n- **Leader Election Trigger**: Election occurs when no heartbeat received within ElectionTimeout (ElectionTicks × TickMs milliseconds)\\n- **Pre-Vote Optimization** (server/config/config.go): Reduces disruptive elections when nodes rejoin; candidates first ask for votes without updating term\\n- **Initial Election Tick Advance**: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to accelerate initial leader election (configurable via --initial-election-tick-advance flag)\\n\\n**Election Timeout Calculation** (server/config/config.go):\\n- ElectionTimeout = ElectionTicks × TickMs (default: 10 ticks × 100ms = 1 second)\\n- Automatic adjustment on server restart to prevent disruptive re-elections\\n\\n**Client-Facing Election API** (server/etcdserver/api/v3election/):\\n- **Campaign**: Place a candidate in the election, wait for previous leader's deletion via watchDeletes()\\n- **Proclaim**: Leader updates its value in the election using transactional compare-and-set with CreateRevision check\\n- **Resign**: Leader voluntarily steps down by deleting its key\\n- **Leader**: Query current election leader by getting first key with WithFirstCreate ordering\\n- **Observe**: Stream ordered leader proclamations as they occur\\n\\nThe gRPC service (v3election.proto) wraps concurrency.Election client through server-side session management.\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n1. **Leader Failure Detection**: Followers detect leader absence when heartbeat messages stop arriving\\n2. **Timeout-Triggered Election**: After ElectionTimeout, followers become candidates and request votes\\n3. **Consensus-Based Selection**: Only candidates with majority votes become leaders (Raft guarantees)\\n4. **Automatic Log Replication**: New leader pulls missing log entries from followers before committing\\n5. **ensureLeadership()** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Verifies leadership via linearizable read; checks raftStatus().Lead equals local MemberID\\n6. **Leadership Transfer**: Graceful handoff when leader steps down\\n\\n**Raft Message Transport** (server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/transport.go):\\n- HTTP/2 based peer-to-peer transport for Raft messages\\n- LeaderStats tracks replication progress to followers\\n- Separate optimized stream for heartbeat AppendEntries messages from leaders\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Distributed lease with API-based storage | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease objects (etcd or external) | In-memory Raft log + persistent WAL |\\n| **Leader Detection** | Polling-based (RetryPeriod) | Heartbeat timeouts (ElectionTicks) |\\n| **Failover Time** | Configurable (LeaseDuration, default 15s) | Bounded by ElectionTimeout (default 1s) |\\n| **Consistency** | Eventual consistency via API | Strong consistency via Raft quorum |\\n| **Scalability** | Limited by API server throughput | Peer-to-peer consensus independent of API |\\n| **Election Coordination** | Sequential leasing with renewal | Parallel voting with quorum requirement |\\n| **Monitoring** | Via LeaderElectionRecord metadata | Via Raft metrics and LeaderStats |\\n\\n### Election State Tracking\\n\\n**Kubernetes LeaderElectionRecord** fields:\\n- HolderIdentity: Current leader ID\\n- AcquireTime: When leadership was acquired\\n- RenewTime: Last renewal timestamp\\n- LeaseDurationSeconds: Lease validity period\\n- LeaderTransitions: Count of leadership changes\\n- PreferredHolder: Next leader candidate (coordinated election)\\n- Strategy: Election strategy being used\\n\\n**etcd Raft Election** state:\\n- raftStatus.Lead: Current leader node ID\\n- raftStatus.Term: Current election term\\n- raftStatus.State: Node's state (Follower/Candidate/Leader)\\n- Raft log: Command sequence establishing consensus\\n- Lease ID: Associated session lease for key holding\\n\\n### Failover and Re-Election Triggers\\n\\n**Kubernetes Triggers:**\\n1. Lease.RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds < current time\\n2. Explicit release (ReleaseOnCancel=true on context cancel)\\n3. Failed Update operations\\n4. LeaderTransitions threshold (coordinated election mode)\\n\\n**etcd Triggers:**\\n1. No heartbeat messages within ElectionTimeout\\n2. Leadership transfer request (Leader.TransferLeadership)\\n3. Configuration changes (membership changes trigger re-election)\\n4. Explicit resignation via Election.Resign() API\\n\\nBoth systems ensure safe, deterministic leadership transitions through either time-based leasing (k8s) or consensus voting (etcd), with proper handling of network partitions and cascading failures.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
